Operation\n\n1.\n\nJSC-l0013\n"\n\nSCOPE\n\n1.1\n\nGeneral. This document specifies the Johnson Space\n(JSC) Mission Control Center (MCC) systems required to\nmonitor and control Shuttle orbital test flights.\nCent~r\'s\n\nThis document defines MtC systems, both hardware and software,\ntheir configurations, and the extent of their implementation to\nbe accomplished for the Orbital Flight Test (OFT) timeframe. The\nOFT timeframe is considered to be through the sixth OFT flight.\nThis specification, therefore, includes certain implementations\nand transistion requirements that must occur to keep the MCC\nfunctionally ready for all phases of the Space Transportation\nSystem (STS) Program.\n2.\n\nAPPLICABLE DOCUMENTS\n\n2.1 General. The MCC Shuttle OFT System shall provide\nfacilities for flight control and data systems personnel to monitor\nand control the Shuttle flights from launch (tower clear) to rollout (wheels stopped on runway). It shall also support the preparation for flight (flight planning, flight controller and crew\ntraining, and integrated vehicle and network testing activities).\nThe MCC Shuttle OFT System shall provide for monitoring and control\nof specific payloads assigned to JSC.\nEmphasis during OFT shall be on the Shuttle system performance\nwith extensive real-time system monitoring performed in the MCC\nto assure crew safety, mission success, and qualification of the\nShuttle onboard systems. As the Shuttle becomes operational, t~e\nMCC support emphasis shall shift from basic systems monitoring\nto payload monitoring, data management, and multiple flight support.\nThe MCC Shuttle OFT System defined in this specification shall pro-.\nvide for all support requirements as defined in the MGG Level A .\nRequirements for Shuttle, Vol. 1: OFT, dated 10 October 1975.\nGeneral support requirements shall be as follows:\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nOrbiter systems monitoring and command\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nTrajectory monitoring and control\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nInflight data acquisition and data information extraction\nnecessary for execution of above functions\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nCommunication\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nMCC System development tools\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\n\'0\n\nTrajectory determination and navigation\n\nSimulation and training.\n\n"7fU-"""I\n\nI\n\nGuidance, targeting, and command\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nI\n\ni\n,\n\ni\n\nI\nI\n\n!\nI-\n\nt F\n\n-,\n\n((\n\n:.-.\n\n-,\n\n~:~\n\n. ;\n\nWDL.. 7321 11/73\n\nPAGE\n\n21\n\nr\n\n"~~~TL\n\n,\n\n...,\n\nr\n\n\'.\n\n~.\n\nt\n\ni.\n\n;/\n\nAeronutronic ~\n\nJSC-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Information Systems Operation\n\n3.1\n\nIntroduction.\n\n\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\n0\n.\n\n.\'\n\n(Continued)\n\nThe MCC Shuttle OFT System configuration shall be based on three\nmajor support systems as shown in figure 1. These support systems\nare the Communication Interface System (CIS), the Data Computation\nComplex (DCC) and the Display and Control System (DeS), all of\nwhich may interface wlth, and share processing facilities with,\nother applications processing supporting current Mec programs.\nOther applications processing shall include:\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nSoftwar~\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nLarge Area Crop Inventory Experiment (LACIE)\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nApollo Lunar Science Experiment Package (ALSEP)\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nProduction Processor System (PPS)\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nData Retrieval and Formatting Technique (DRAFT)\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nMedical Information Computer System (MEDIC5).\n\nDevelopment \'Lab (SDL)\n\n3.1.1 Purpose of the MCC. The MCC shall provide centralized\ncontrol of the NASA Space Shuttle OFT from launch through orbital\nflight, entry, and landing until the Orbiter comes to a stop on\nthe run~ay. This control shall include the functions of vehicle\nmanagement in the area of hardware configuration (verification),\nflight planning, communication and instrumentation configuration\nmanagement, traj ectory, software and con.\'~umables; payloads management; flight safety; and verification of test conditions/environment.\n3.1.2 Operations. The TDRSS\nis expected to reduce the GSTDN support required for Shuttle as\nit becomes operational. It shall consist of two satellites placed\nin a geosynchronous equatorial orbit to give maximum earth orbit\ncoverage to spacecrafts at orbital altitudes up to approximately\n2700 nmi (5000 km), and one primary ground station, optimally\nlocated for viewing the two satellites.\n3.2 MCC Shuttle Data Flow. The following paragraphs describe the major data flows within the MCC in support of Shutt10\noperations. Primary data flows shall be:\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\n,-~-\n\nTrajectory\n\nVideo\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\n",\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n0\n\n,\n\nTelemetry\n\n:Teletype\n\nCommand\n\nI\ni\n\n!\n\n1\n\nVoice.\n\n1\n!\n\n3.2.1 Telemetry. Telemetry data shall be received by the\nMCC from three sources: GSFC, TDRSS, and the Shuttle Mission\nSimulator (SMS) in JSC Bldg. S. Shuttle operational instrumentation (01) telemetry data shall arrive at the Mec independently\nor simultaneously from one or any combination of these sources\nover a 1.544 Mb/s interface. Data shall be routed into the MCC\nvia common carrier interfaces into the MCC modulator/demodulator\n(MODEM) and Line Driver/Termination Equipment. The data shall\nnormally be iouted through this facility into a GSFC network\ndemultj,p1exer where it shall be demultiplcxed and routed.\n\ni,\n\n;i,\n\n:, )I~____________--=-~~_---\'\nWDL 7UI \'1/73\n\nPAGE\n\n24\n\n1\n\nj\nj\n\n1\n\n~\nr\n\nI\n\n~[~-"\n\nI\nI\n\n;\n\nt\n\nI\n\n.\\ :\n\n1\n\nI\n\nAeronutronic\n\nT\n\n~.\n\n_\n\n,\n\nr\n\n....\n\n---~I\n\n~l\n\n\'r~\'\n\nr\n\n}\n\nj\n\nJSC-l0013\n\n-\'eronutronic Ford Corporation;\nSpace Infonnation Systems Operation\n\n3.2.1\n\nTelemetry.\n\n(Continued)\n\nData not addressed to JSC shall be routed from the demultiplexer\nunit into a GSFC multiplexer unit for output relay to other destinations, i. e., White Sands (WHS). All incoming JSC data shall be"\nrouted through the Digital Data Line Switch to the Network\nCommunications Interface Common (NCIC) unit of the Network\nInterface Processor (NIP) in blocked data format (BDF). See\nfigure 2.\n.\nThe NCIC shall accept the wideband data (WBD) input and prepare\nthe data for further processing by the Telemetry Processing Computer (TPC). The NCr shall perform the required communications\nmanagement-type functions including synchronization, poly-code\nchecking, header processing, error statusing, and selective\nmessage handling. In addition, the NCr shall perform air to\nground (A/G) subframe synchronization, ground receipt time tagging, digit~l voice stripping (if required), and A/G error statusing. Data from the NCI/TPC Subsystems shall be output to the\nShuttle Data Processing Complex (SDPC), Analog Event Subsystem\n(AES), and Dum\xc2\xb7p Data Playback (DDP) Subsystem for proc~ssing.\n\nJ\nJ\n\nTelemetry data shall be Tecorded in raw form by the WBD Recorder/\nReproducer Subsystem. This data shall provide a history of all\nincoming data into the Mec.\nThe TPC\' s shall provide an output of analog and bilevel. event\ndata, stripped from the incoming data stream, tq the AES for\ndirect display on recorder and/or light displays.\n1\ni\n\nI\n\nL\n\nTelemetry Gata received from the STDN consisting of dumped spacecraft recorder data shall require additional processing after\npassing through the NCI to establish a proper data relationship.\nDump data may enter the system in either the forward or reverse\nmode with dead spaces intermixed in the stream. Processing functions accomplished within the SD~C shall\nbe:\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nCommand verification and history tabulation\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nDownlink control\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nTelemetry delogs\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nReal-time computation and analysis\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nEngineering unit (EU) conversion\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nData presentation\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nScaling\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\n"\n\nCalibration and limit sensing\n\nTelemetry History Report in Formatted Tabulations (THRIFT)\nlogging.\n\nThe SDPC shall provide telemetry data-derived products, (i.e.,\ndisplays, log tap~s, event lights, alarms, console readout devices)\nto MCC users. Telemetry data shall also be provided to the 360/75\nTrajectory Processor via the System Configuration Unit (SCU) and\nSystem Selector Unit/System Selector Extension Unit (SSU/SSEU) for\nuse in trajectory and tracking computations.\n\nWDL 7321 11/73\n\nPAGE\n\n27\n\n---r --\'.!\n\nr\n\nI\n\nI\nf1\n\n.\n\n--l~~-~ -\'~.-.\n\n\xc2\xb7--~l~~~-!~--\xc2\xb7\n\n,\n\nr\n\n1\n\nt\n/\n\nf~\n\nI\xc2\xb7\n\n. Command data from the MCC shall be initiated\nat the console command modules or manual entry devices (MED\'s).\nCommand requests shall be passed from the command modules via\nthe Command/Computer Input Multiplexer (C/CIM) and SCD to the SDPC,\nwhere the command requests shall be coded and commands generated.\nTrajectory data shall be generated by the 360/75 and passed\nto the SDPC for command generation. Simulation command data shall be\nrouted to Bldg. 5 from these same units to simulate either or\nboth GSTDN and TDRSS uplinks.\nNetwork management commands shall be transmitted to the remote\nsites from the MCC and shall be used to control and monitor remote\nsite ground functions. The MCC shall be required to provide support to Shuttle in a variety of configurations\nin normal and contingency operations. Mission phases identified\nfor support are:\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nLaunch\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nLanding\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nAbort/Contingency\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nFlight Simulations\n\n._ Nominal On-Orbit Operations.\nEach support area imposes operational restrictions upon the MCC\nand the needed .tools must be available to meet these conditions.\nThe following assumptions are made concerning MCC support for\nthese mission phases:\na.\n\nAll MCC resources shall be available for support as\nneeded.\n\nb.\n\nNo routine simulation shall be conducted during critical\nphases.\n\nc.\n\nThose resources not committed to mission support shall be\navailable on a 30-minute callup basis.\n\nWOL 73Z1 11/73\n\nPAGE\n\n33\n\n"-r --"\n\nt\n\nr\n\nI\n\n..\n\nr\n\n,\n\nr\n\n~;\n\nJ\n\nt\n\n-\\-_._\n\n...\n\n---"- -~-\'\n\n,\n1\n\nl\n\n\xc2\xb7Aeronutronic f\'liD\n\n-\\\n\n"\n\n"1r\n\nr\n\nf\n\n1\n\nJSC-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Information Systems Operation\n\no\n\n1\n\n3.3.1 Launch. The launch mission phase is considered critical and shall require dedicated online and dynamic standby resources\nin all areas where failures could disrupt or degrade mission support\ncapabilities. Operations shall be conducted in such a manner that the best available source of data\nwill be processed for output. Data integrity must be maintained\nat all times.\n3.3.2 Landing. All resources listed in paragraph 3.3.1\nabove, except countdown and status data and IP data shall be\nnecessary for support during this mission phase. Non-nominal operations such as\naborts and on-orbit contingencies shall require fast, efficient\nreflex action by the MCC. Such activities shall require that any\nand all resources which lend themselves to problem solutions and\npredictions be available if required. JSC resources such as\nsimulations; math models, and mock-ups which can be use~ to assist in decisicin making shall be on call. S~ch ~ctivities may\nrequire that all nonmission-related activities cease and the\nresources they use be committed to-mission support. Nonmission\nresources such as LACIE, ALSEP, SDL, DRAFT, and other such activities are prime candidates in this area.\n\n0. ..\n.\xc2\xb7\n.\n\nj\ni1\n\ni\nj\n\n1\n\n1\n\n3.3.4 Flight Simulation. The capability to support realistic\nShuttle OFT flight simulations shall be provided. Input simulated\nflight data shall originate in the SMS in Bldg. 5 and be transmitted to the MCC. All simulation data shall be in the same\nformat as mission data received from or transmitted to the GSTDN\nor TDRSS. The SMS shall simulate not only booster/Orbiter/payload\nfunctions but also the GSTDN/TDRSS functions.\nTypes of simulations to be supported shall include launch, landing,\nand orbital. Simulations shall be required to present high fidelity telemetry, command, tracking, and voice data to the MCC. Simulation exercises shall cover both nominal and abnormal mission\nsituations.\n\n1\n\nI\n\nI\n1\n\nWOL 7321 11/73\n\nPAGE\n\n36\n\nr\n\nr\n\nT~\xc2\xb7\n\n..\n\n-~\n\n-------\n\n--\'"\'\'\'\'-\'\'\'I!\'i\'\'---\n\n,\n\n.\n\n1\n\nI\n\n1\n\n--I\n\n...\n\n..~\n\n$-\n\n-I\nI\n\nI\n\nr\n\n{\n\nI\n\nL\n\n/\n\nJffi\n.\n\nAeronutronic ~\n\n:Jt\n\n~.,\n~\n.\n\nI\n\nJSC-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Infonnation Systems Operation\n\n3.3.4\n\nFlight Simulation.\n\n(Continued)\n\nNo simulation-unique hardware or software shall reside in the MCC;\nsimulation control consoles and all special data faulting equipment shall exist external to the MCC (except simulation monitor\nconsoles).\n3.3.5 Nominal On-Orbit Operations. The capability to support\nnominal on-orbit operations shall be provided by the NCC. Those\nresources listed in paragraph 3.3.1 except for the DCU-R and CASRS\nshall be necessary for support during this mission phase. MCC\nsupport operations shall include computer complexes and operations support functions in the areas of trajectory and mission\nplanning, command, telemetry, communications, and display required to accomplish command and control of the Orbiter vehicle\nand its attached payloads.\n3.4 MCC Functional Allocations. The functional requirements,\nas defined in the MGG Level A Requirements for Shuttle~ Vol. 1:\nOFT~ shall be allocated to three MCC systems (see figure 6):\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nCommunications Interface System (CIS)\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nData Computation Complex (nCC)\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nDisplay and Control System (DCS).\n\n3.4.1 Communication Interface System. The CIS (as shown in\nfigure 7) shall perform the functions of providing voice and data\ncommunications within the MeC, and between the MCC and external\ncircuits. It\nshall include capability to interface and reconfigure the circuits and provide measurement of\ncircuit performance.\nb.\n\nNetwork Interface Processor (NIP). The NIP shall\nprovide processing of incoming network data to the\nextent of determining data validity and quality;\nextracting voice data,. tracking and site status,\nconfiguration data, and telemetry data; and preprocessing individual vehicle data for transmission to\nthe SDPC.\n\nc.\n\nNetwork Output Multiplexer (NOM). The NOM shall\nprovide interleaving of digital voice and SDPC\noutput data for transmission to the network. Voice\nand data interleaving shall be accomplished when\noutputting to TDRSS; data shall be outpu~ only\nwhen transmitting to GSTDN. Interleaving shall\nnot be performed for network management commands\noutput to the network.\n\nd.\n\nDump Data Processor (DDP). The DDP Subsystem shall\nprovide a chronologically ordered output from a\nforward/reverse mode, high bit rate (HBR) spacecraft telemetry data dump.\n\ne.\n\nVoice Communication Subsyst~m (VCS). The VCS\nshall provide voice communications among MCC operating positions, and between these operating positions and other external ground support locations.\nIt shall provide PA coverage in the MCC, and A/G\ncommunications with the Orbiter, both analog through\nGSTDN and digital through TDRSS.\n\n\xc2\xb7~l\n\n\\~~L-I__________..:.-________~~~____. . .\nWDL 7321 11/73\n\nPAGE\n\n40\n\n.-\n\nJ\n\nf~--\n\n,\n\nI\n\nr\n\ni\n\n-.~~~\n\n.\n\n"""\'_.. ,- --\'-\n\n,\n\nj\n\n-r\n\nAeronutronic E!D\n\n--\'-1\'r\n\nf\n\nJSC-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\n\nSpace Informatilll Systems Operation\n\n3.4.1\n\nCommunication Interface System.\nf.\n\n(Continued)\n\nConsolidated Communications Recording Facility (CCRF).\nThe CCRFshall provide historical recording of all\ndata and selected voice communications entering or\nleaving the MCC.\n\n3.4.1.1 External Interfaces. MCC Shuttle operations shall\nrequire that digital data, video, and voice communications be\nexchanged with a number of locations external to the MCC. The\nexternal locations may be on the JSC premises or may be remotely\nlocated. The following locations and interfaces shall be required\nfor the Shuttle OFT timeframe.\na.\n\nFlight Operations Interfaces. These interfaces\nshall be to the launch areas, the landing areas,\nand the o~-orbit tracking network data sources.\nAll shall provide real-time support of specific\nmission activities.\n(1) Launch Area. It shall be a direct KSC/JSC\ncircuit.\n\n(c)\n\nWDL. 73Z1 1 \'/73\n\nVoice. Approximately 40 full-duplex 3\nkHz voice circuits shall be required for\ncoordination purposes. These shall be\ndir.ect JSC/KSC circuits including A/G.\n\nData. Three receive-only high-speed data\ncircuits shall be required from KSC. One\ncircuit shall provide meteorological data\n\nPAGE\n\n41\n\n-f\nj\n\nr\n,\n\nr----\n\ni\n\n-\n\nj\n\nI.\n\nr~---\n\n,\n\nI\n\nr--\'---\n\nAeronutronlc ~\n\n-"-1\n\n\'1\n\nr\n\nf\n\nJSC-10013\n\nAeronutrcnlc Ford Corporation\n~ hformation Systems Operation\n\n3.4.1.1\n\nExternal Interfaces.\n\n(Continued)\n\n(wind profiles); another shall provide\nlaunch/landing radar data from the ETR\nRTCS via KSC; and the third shall provide\ncountdown and status data. Landing during the OFT timeframe shall utilize KSC and Edwards AFB as\nprimary sites, with Hickam AFB and Anderson AFB\nas secondary landing sites.\n(NOTE: For emergency operations, SO contingency fields capable\nof handling the vehicle may be used. The transition period from Shuttle\nOrbital Flight Testing (OFT) to Shuttle Operations (OPS) shall\nbring about major changes to MCC operations and resources. The\ntime period from second quarter 1980, to fourth quarter 1981 is\ndenoted as "Transition Period" for the Svace Shuttle Program.\nI t is noted, however, that the "Trans i tion" of the .MCC to support Shuttle activities is currently in progress and shall continue to evolve until Space Transportation System (STS) maturity.\nThe ~ICC shall continue to support other programs while the development of Shuttle continues.\n\nChanges which are expected to occur over the -"Transition" period\nare:\na.\n\nTDRSS Operational. TDRSS is expected to be launched\nin FY 1980. The initial system will be limited to\nS-band capability. High-bit rate Ku-band capability\nwilI not be available immediately. During first\n(.~n.uTter CY 1981, full bi t rate capabili ty is expected to be implemented for operational support.\n\nb.\n\nShuttle Online Data Base. The MCC will implement\nan online data base in support of Shuttle during\nthe OFT/OPS transition period. The data base must\nbe operational at the beginning of the OPS timeframe. This implies that implementation of this\nsystem should begin in second quarter 1979. T~e\ndata base is projected to be part of the SDPC.\n\nI\n\n!\n\nWDL 7321 11/73\n\nPAGE\n\n78\n\n\xc2\xb70","\n\n1\n\n"..-.~-.\n\n!\n!\n\nI\n\nj\n\n-~.-~\n\n~\n\n-r~\n\nr~-\n\n,\n\nI\n\nI\n\n1\n\nAeronutronic ~\n\nr\n\n~~r\n\n!\n\n-;1\n\n,\n\n1\n\nJSC-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpac~ Infonnation Systems Operation\n\n3.8\n\nOFT/OPS Transition.\n\n(Continued)\n\nc.\n\nTerminal Applications Support System (TASS) Implemented Within SDPC. Output Mul tiplexer (Nm.O Subsystem. The\nNOM shall accept outgoing network data from the\nSDPC, add digital voice when required, and interface the STDN (both GSTDN and TDRSS).\n\nd.\n\nDump Data Processing Subsystem (DDPS).\nThe DDPS\nshall accept high-rate dumps of onboard data and\nprovide reformatting and reordering of data segments to permit MCC processing.\n\ne.\n\nVoice Communications Subsystem eVCS). The VCS\nshall provide voice communications among MCC\noperating positions, and between these operating\npositions and external locations.\nIt shall also\n\'provide public address coverage of the MCC and A!G\ncommunications with the Orbiter.\n\ni\n,\n\'j\n11\n\n\'I1\n\nJ\n\\\n\nf.\n\n-\'\n\nConsolidated Communications Recording Facility\n(CCRF). The NOM shall pro,vide the output interface between the MCC and the STDN. The NOM\nshall accept data blocks containing commands, acquisition data,\nsite commands, etc. from the SDPC via the MBI and transmit the\nda~a block serially in the NASCOM format to the selected port of\nthe GSTDN Multiplexer (MUX). The NOM shall accept data blocks\ncontaining Orbiter command or computer load data from the SDPC\nvia the MBI, and shall time-division multiplex the SDPC data with\ndigital voice, digital text, and graphics data to provide continuous synchronous serial Shuttle uplink formats to the TDRSS\nMUX. (See figure 20).\n4.2.3.1 GSTDN Block Transfers. The NOM shall accept output\ndata blocks from the SDPC, provide double buffering of the SDP\nblocks, and serialize the data for transmission to the GSTDN ~IUX.\nThe NOM shall route data to one port (GSFC) of the GSTDN MUX for\npre-TDRSS OFT and to six ports (GSFC, plus five sites) of the\nGSTDN MUX for post-TDRSS OFT and OPS.\nThe SDP output block to the NOM shall contain only NASCOM header\nand output data. The NOM shall provide fixed NASCOM header and\ndata fill required to complete a 4.8K bit NASCOM block. The NO~I\nshall format and output one NASCOM block for each SDP input block.\nI\n\nI\nI\n\nI\n\nI\nI\nI\n\nThe NOM shall provide GSTDN block data output hardware to support\noperations and simulations, and to back up the operational hardware, as a mlnlmum. NOM internal hardware shall be manually assigned to operational or simulation output ports. Routing of\nSDPC data to NOM internal functions shall be provided by an SDP\nROUTING field in the data block, designating the NOM output port\n(MUX input port) for the selected block.\n\nWOL 7321 11/73\n\nPAGE\n\n112\n\nj\n\n1\n\n\xc2\xb71\n\nI\n\n1\n\n"1\n\nj\n\xc2\xb71\n\n,\n\nI.\n\n:oiiil\'F\'\n\n\'::"\'.. There shall be five types of voice\ncircuits as defined in the following paragraphs.\na.\n\nLocal Conference Loops. These loops shall comprise\n4-wire conference circuits providing 2-way communications and monitoring capability for all stations\non the loop. Other CCS loops cannot be connected\nto the conference loop, nor shall this loop require\nsignalling. There shall be a total of 204 local\nConference loops.\n\nb.\n\nlntersite Conference Loops. The DCC shall provide\ncomputational, peripheral, and switching capability which will\nsupport the requirements derived from the OFT Level A Requirements\nfor the Shuttle Ground Data System (SGDS).\nOther applications\n(e.g., SDL, LACIE, ALSEP) shall also be supported by the DCC.\nThe DCC shall ,be composed of the Mul tibus Interface (MBl) , Shuttle\nData Processing Complex (SDPC), 360/75 Computer Complex, UNIVAC\n494 Computer Complex, and the DCC-to-MCC Systems Configuration\nand Switching Equipment.\n4.3.1 Multibus Capability. The MBI is an interface device\nthat shall allow, at a minimum, 11 computers (5 TPC\'s and 5 SDPC\'s)\nto be interconnected in nearly any manner. EaLh computer shall\nhave the capability to both receive and transmit data simultaneously, and to transmit data to one or two devices simultaneously.\nHowever, a computer shall not simultaneously receive data from\nmUltiple devices. The data transfers shall take place on five\nfull-duplex buses at a rate of 500,000 bytes (8 bits/byte) per\nsecond. The MBI hardware can be divided into three different\nfunctional sections:\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nAdapter and Bus\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nConfigurator and Controller (CC)\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nSelf-Tester and Maintenance Panel.\n\nAll of the hardware shall be redundant making the MBI an entirely\nredundant system.\n4.3.1.1 Adapter and Bus. A unique adapter shall be made for\neach kind of device connected to the MBI. At a minimum there shall\nbe two unique adapter designs, one for the TPC and one for the\nSDPC. If any more devices are added, they too shall rpquire a\nunique adapter.\n\ni\n\n\xc2\xb71\n\'j\n\ni\n\nI\n\nj\n\n1\n\nI\n\nWDL 7321 1/76\n\nPAGE\n\n148\n\nr\n\nI\n\n>\n\nf\n\nL\n\n~\n\n~-.......-,-\n\n~--\n\n,\n\nj\n\n1\n\nAeronutronic ED\n\n~\n\n1\n\n.\n\n~\xc2\xb7I~"~\n\n1.-...\n\nr\n\n(\n\n1\n\nAdapter and Bus.\n\n(Continued)\n\na.\n\nLevel Conversion. The adapter shall convert computer voltage levels to TTL levels and TTL levels\nto computer levels.\n\nh.\n\nWord Conversion. The adapter shall convert the\n~omputer word to an 8-bit word for transmission\nover the bus.\n\nc.\n\nBus Transmission Rate. The maximum transmission\nrate shall be SOOK bytes per second.\n\nd.\n\nError Detection. the adapter shall attach four bits\nof Hamming code t(~ each word transmitted over the\nbus. The Hamming code is an error detection and\ncorrection code which can detect and correct one\nerror, and can detect the presence of two or more\nerrors.\n\ne.\n\n.0\n\n\'I\nl\n\nJ8C-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Fori Corporation\n,3pace Infonnation Systems Operation\n\n4.3.1.1\n\nor\n\nNumber of Buses. The computer shall communicate with the CC through the adapter. The CC\nshall scan the adapters with the adapter select\nlines, and monitor the auxiliary control lines to\ndetermine the status of the adapter and whether\nadapter wants to transmit data to the CC. If the\nCC wants to transmit to the adapter, it shall do so\nover the same lines with a separate line indicating\nthat the adapter is to receive.\nThe types of messages to be sent from the adapter to\nthe CC shall be origination code, destination code,\npriority code, number of words to be transmitted,\nand status of transmitter and receiver.\nThe types of messages to be sent from the CC to\nadapter shall be adapter select, bus select, CC\ntransmitting, configure, status of destination\nadapter, and transmit status to host computer.\n\nI.\n\nI\n\n4.3.1.1.2 Local Control. The local control on each adapter shall\ntake the external control lines coming into it and reduce them to\nthe four necessary control lines for bus operation. The local\ncontrol shall take the four control lines coming in on the bus\nand control lines from host computer and CC and manipulate them\nso as to give the CC or host computer the status of that ad~pter.\n\n1\n\xc2\xb71\n\n4.3.1.2 Configurator and Controller (CC). When the SDP\'s are configured in a MOC/\nDSC configuration, a method shall te available to\nsignal the two systems that a se1ec~over will occur,\ni,e., the MOC shall become DSC and the DSC shall become MOC. This shall be accomplished by providing\nsignals to the systems involved indicating selectover will occur and also indicating the status of\nthe selectover. To indicate a selectover is to\noccur, a positive level (logical one) shall be sent\nto both the MOC and DSC. Once the SDP\'s receive\nthis se1ectover interrupt, both systems must suspend\ntheir output operations until se1ectover has occurred; i.e., any message that has started from\n~ither computer shall be completed, but no new outputs shall be started. Under normal conditions,\nrelays shall switch the outputs after 200 ms. In\naddition to the one interrupt line, each system\n$hal1 be provided with three status lines which will\npresent the status (improper, incomplete; or proper)\nof the se1ectover. The status\' shall be presented\nby putting a ONE or ZERO in various combinations on\nthe three lines. All four lines and drivers shall\nbe GFE, and the signals shall originate from GFE.\n\nJ\n\nI\n\ni\n!\n\n4.3.2.2.5 SDP/SDP Interface. Each 360/75\nsystem is equipped with a 2075 J CPU which contains 1,048,576\nbytes of main storage. The cycle time of this storage is 750 ns.\nIn addition to the main core storage each system is equipped \\vi th\ntwo 2361-2 Large Core Storage (LCS) units which provide an additional 4,194,304 bytes of storage. Using interleaving techniques,\na cycle time of 4 ~s can be obtained. System E uses different\nhardware (Ampex ECM) other than IBM 2361-2 LCS and is able to obtain a 2 ~s cycle time.\nEach 360/75 uses channels to transfer data between I/O devices\nand the CPU. The channel relieves the CPU of the burden of communicating directly with I/O devices and permits CPU operations\nto proceed concurrently with I/O operations. The 360/75 system\nhas t\\vO types of channels, a multiplexer channel (MC) (2870) and\na selector channel (SC\'s) (2860). One 2860-2 and one 2870-1 is\nattached to each 360/75.\nThe 360/75 2860 is implemented with two SC\'s (1 and 2). SC2 is\ncapable of an I/O rate of 2.4 megabytes per second if the SC and\ncontrol unit are within 10 feet of the CPU. The SC operates in\na burst mode only. In this mode one device monopolizes the I/O\ninterface and stays connected to the channel for the duration of\nan operation. Normally high-speed devices are connected to this\ntype of channel. SC1 operates at a maximu~ I/O rate 1.2 megabytes\nper second.\nThe 2870 can operate in the burst mode or a multiplexer mode. In\nthe multiplex mode, an MC can operate with more than one I/O device at a time. The 2870\'s implemented for each 360/75 have one\nMe and two selector subchanne1s (SSC\'s) which allow the HC to have\na maximum I/O rate 66 kilobytes per second and SSC\'s to have a\nmaximum I/O rate of 180 kilobytes per second. Normally, mediumand low-speed devices are connected to the 2870\'s.\n1\n\nWOL. 732\' \'/76\n\nPAGE\n\n168\n\nI~\n\n!\n\n"T\n\nr---\'~\'\n\n,\nI\n\n\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7l~\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\n\nI\n\nJ\n\nI\n\n/.\n\nAeronutronic\n\n~\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Infonnation Systems Operation\n\nl)\n\n,\nI\n\n-\n\n-...........\n\n_ _4"~ __\n\n,\n\n. -1\n\n-~r\n\nC\n4\n\ni\n\nt\n\n\\\n\nr\n\nJSC-10013\n\n4.3.3.2 360/75 Computer Complex Interface Capability. The Configuration Controller shall provide sufficient controls to allow the entry and\nverification of data paths through the SCU, inject and retrieve\ntest data, localize failures, provide a scan of the matrices, and\nprovide the resulting status to the advisory printer. The Configuration Controller shall be capable of two operational modes,\nsemiautomatic or manual, as selected by the Configuration Control\nConsole. Overall system management shall be provided which is\nindependent of the mode of operations selected by the Configuration Control Console.\n4.3.5~1.4\n\nSwitch Matrix. Each switch matrix shall consist\nof a switching element and an interface element, The switching\nelement shall provide the switching of the data lines; the interface element shall convert all data lines to voltage levels compatible with the switching element as well as providing certain\ncontrol, test and monitoring features.\n\n_\n\n"\n\nf\n.-\'\n\na.\n\nSwitching Element. Each switch matrix shall provide\nfor the connection of anyone of 100 inputs to any\none or more, up to a maximum of 10,\'0\xc2\xa3 any 100 outputs. Each input and output shall consist of four\nlevels. Three of these levels shall propagate\nthrough the switch matrix from the input to the output; the fourth level shall propagate from the output to the input. The switch matrix shall accomplish\nthe intersections using 3000 input/output intersections (~rosspoints). Each switch matrix shall be\ndivided into three groups. Interconnection of one\ncrosspoint in each matrix group shall be required\nto establish a data path through the switch matrix.\nThe crosspoints in a matrix group shall be individually addressable from the Configuration Controller. To complete a path through a switch matrix,\nthree addresses shall be required. Each address\nreceived by a switch matrix shall be encoded and\nreturned to the Configuration Controller for verification before a crosspoint is opened or closed.\nRedundant switch matrix control lines shall be provided.\n\n0\xc2\xb7.\xc2\xb7\' ,\n-.\n\nPAGE\n\n201\n\n-\n\nr\n\n!\n\nI\n\nf ----\n\n--I~\' --~-l\n\ni\n\n,\n\n\'\n\ni\n\nI\n\n)\n\n~--:-l\n\nJ\n\nr\n\nf\n,\n\n,\n\n1\n\nJSC-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Infonnation Systems Operation\n\nh.\n\n-1-"\n\n"\n\nf\n\nI\n\nSwitch Matrix.\n\n-~\n\nj\n\nAeronutronic ~\n\n4.3.5.1.4\n\n"f----\n\n(Continued)\n\nInterface Element. The interface element shall provide compatibility between the two switch matrices\nof the SCD and all data facilities external to and\ninterfacing with the SCD. The interface element\nfor each matrix shall consist of 100 input circuits\n(ports) mounted on terminator cards and 100 output\ncircuits (ports) mounted on driver cards. Each input and output port shall consist of four levels.\nThe SCU shall allow each external device to utilize\none or more of these levels which are arbitrarily\ndesignated as data, clock, ready, and Ready-toReceive (RTR). Each input port shall be capable of\naccepting three signal levels from the external\nequipment and shall be capable of transmitting one\nsignal level to the external equipment. Likewise,\neach output port shall be capable of transmitting\nthree signal levels to and receiving one signal\nlevel from the external equipment. There shall be\ntwo ports of the same type mounted on an interface\ncard. There shall be three types of functional interfa\'ce cards and one nonfunctional interface card.\nThe functional interface cards shall be the widebanu MODH!, high - speed MODEr.!, and 494/360 interface\nadapter terminator cards and driver cards. The nonfunctional interface card shall be a dummy terminator\nand driver. The dummy interface card shall have\nonly the necessary circuitry to allow completion of\nthe test data paths. All circuits interfacing between the SCU and the different computer systems\nshall be termed processor-oriented circuits (POC\'s).\nThe SCU shall be capable of allowing two o~ three\nSDP computer systems to simultaneously support a\nmission. Consequently, crosspoint configurations\ndefining the data paths through the SCU must simultaneously exist within the SCU for the three system\n\n1\n\n1\n\nWOL 7321 ,1/76\n\n"-r--\n\n_ - -I\n\nr\n\n--~r-------~\n\nI\n\nI\n~\n\nI\n\n...\n\n(\n\njD\n\nI\n\nI\ni\n\nAeronutronic E!D\n\nJSC-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Information Systems Operation\n\n~.3.S.I.4\n\nSwitch Matrix.\n\n(Continued)\n\nPOC\'s. Such a crosspoint configuration would allow\nthree sources (each POC) to be connected to a single\nload (circuits external to SDPC). To allow all\nthree systems to actively process data but allow\nonly one system to drive the load, the interface\nelement shall have provisions for a standby signal\nshich will inhibit all POC\'s except the online POC\'s\nwhich will be connected to the load. Any of the\nsystems\' POC\'s\'may be selected to the online position upon command from the control console. Selection of the I/O ports as POC\'s shall be made via\nt\\vO 300-positiort pinboards (100 input and 100 output\npositions per system)\nThe two 300-position pinboards shall supply the standby signal to all ports\nselected by pins as POC\'s. The standby signal shall\ninhibit all three receive levels of the POC input\nport and the one receive level of the POC output\nport, and cause the transmitted level of the input\nport to be constantly active.\nL\n\nEach interface circuit shall consist of four signals,\neach routed through a different level of the crosspoint switch. The DTE shall accept multiples\nof either five bytes for the 36-bit format, or six\nbytes for the 48-bit data format. In 36-bit mode,\nthe four MSB\' s of the first byte of each 5 -by tel\n40-bit wori received from the byte serial adapter\n(BSA) shall be disregarded. The mode of -operation\nshall be switch-selectable on a cluster-by-cluster\nbasis, and the cluster hardware shall be completely\nreini tialized i\\Then switching modes. The DTE. shall\nverify that the total number of bytes received from\nthe DCC in a single message is divisible by five in\nthe 36-bit mode, and is divisible by six in the 48bit mode. A command error is sent to the nec if\nthe correct division is not verified.\nDCC-DTE Data Transfer Rates. The DCCU shall\ncontrol the acceptance or rejection of the computer\ndata appearing at the DTE input interfaces by providing a cluster allocation function. The TV conversion equipshall include the LSR converter, FS-to-NTSC converter, and\ntime base converter [Digital Coherent Video Synchronizer (DCVS)].\n\nm~nt\n\na.\n\nh.\n\n~\n\nl.. ...\n\nFS-to-NTSC Color Converter. The 525-line system\nshall provide for the conversion of spacecraft sequential color video to an NTSC format and simultaneously record this information for OFT editing,\nplayback, and archive. The time base of the incoming FS signal shall be corrected to the Bldg. 30\nsync standards by a Tape Loop or ~olid State Memory\nTim~ Base System before processing into NTSC format.\nThe basic hardware in the FS/NTSC converter shall\nbe a rotating magnetic disk with three flying heads\nthat input through switchable l/2-line delay lines.\nThe control logic shall be arranged so that recording and playback occur in an output sequence compatible with NTSC encoder requirements. The simultaneous red, green, blue (RGB) signal shall be routed\nto an encoder where chrominance and burst are added\nto provide the complete color encoded signal. The\nFS-to-NTSC color converter shall satisfactorily\nsupport all known OPT requirements.\n\n,\ni\n\n......\n\nLSR Converters. The LSR converters shall perform\nthe change from one scan rate to another (945 to\n525 or 525 to 945) through a camera and monitor combination for each converter. The video information\nshall be presented on a monitor at one scan rate\nand picked up ~y a camera operating at the scan rate\nof the display monitors. This arrangement provides\nan economical scan rate conversion with some loss\nin resolution.\n\nJ\n\n--\n\n0. . ,\n.\xc2\xb7\n~\n\n1\n\nc.\n\nTime Base Converter. The DDD\'s shall provide only a sing~~ hardware data path betw6en their\nrespective input~ and the user devices, with the\ninterface between the DDD\'s and user devices being\nhardwired and nonswitchable in real-time. However,\nprovision of multifunction, overlay-type digital\nevent indicator panels for certain DCC-DDD events\n~hall afford an operationally redundant data path\nthrough the DDD\'s and to the user for those particular lamp driven events. This redundancy shall\nbe realized in the following manner. Loss of a\ngiven DDD set and/or its hardwired DDD-to-event\npanel interface shall require the user to select an\navailable blank multifunction panel (nominally on\nthe same console as the original panel) and condition the new panel to accept the requited parameters\nfor display. Program response to the new panel assignment shall cause the original display parameters\nto be routed through the SDD to a new DDD set and\nits corresponding output interface to the newly selected panel. This DDD redundancy shall be available only for the lamp driven events, and shall be\nlimited by the immediate availability of spare mUltifunction panels in the proximity of the original\nnonuseable panel.\n\n\xc2\xb71\n\nj\n\n.i\n\nI\n!\n\n.}\n~\n\n.\n\n~~-,--\n\n. i\'\n\n1\n\nr\n-------------------------------------------------------------~\nWDL. 737.1 1/76\nPAGE 246\n\xe2\x80\xa2.\n\nj\n\n.u\n\nr\n\n\'I\n\nr-I\n\n!\n\n. ~.\n\nT~\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7~\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\n\nI\n"\n\nI\n\n,\n\nl~\xc2\xb7\n\nJSC-IOOI3\n\n4.4.2.6 Analog and Event Distribution (AED). The Console Subsystem shall provide the physical housing for the majority of display and control\nend devices required for direct operator interface with the DCC.\nIt shall consist of functionally-grouped keyboards, digital/event\nindicators and TV monitors mounted in mechanically interlocked\nmultiples of a modular I-bay console.\n\nI\nj\n\n4.4.2.7.1 Functional Requirements. The DSCIM shall provide ESW encoders\nto inform all eight DCCcomputers of GO/NO GO status of each DTE\nchannel.\nIn addition, CAW encoders shall assign a cluster or\ngroup of clusters to a particular DCC computer.\na.\n\nESW Processing. The DSCIM shall provide five ESW\nencoders for accepting 80 individual static level\nGO/NO GO status indications, one each from the 80\nDTE channels. Each of the six encoders shall accept\n16 inputs, and each shall have its contents contained in single 36-bit DSCIM output word to the\nDCC. The DSCIM shall process all six encoder contents, and output all six words in a sequential\norder to the DCC, under the following conditions.\n(1)\n\nt2)\n\nb.\n\nI\nWOL. 7UI 1/76\n\nDTE Status Change. A GO/NO GO status change\non anyone of the 80 ESW inputs to the DSCIM\nshall cause the DSCIM to output the entire\n6-word ESW sequence.\nESW Request From DCC. Each of the eight DCC\ncomputers shall provide, -via its DTE interface\nunit (figure 42), an ESW request interface signal to the DSCIM. These eight ESW request lines\nshall be DR\'ed within the DSCIM; an active request signal on anyone of the eight shall\ncause the DSCnr to output the entire 6-word\nESW sequence to all eight DCC computers. NOTE:\nThe ESW request condition shall also cause the\nDSCIM to output eight CAW\'s in sequence\n(preceding) the ESW\'s, as defined in paragraph\nb below.\n\n-\n\nCAW Processing. The DSCIM shall provide eight CAW\nencoders, each capable of accepting 20 parallel input lines from the DCCU. These inputs shall contain static logic level representations of DCCU\nallocations of DTE equipment, with each encoder\nhaving a fixed correlation to a DCC computer. Whenever a service request\nis detected from an input device, further scanning\nshall be inhibited and the DSCIM shall latch onto\nthe data lines of the requesting device until transmission is complete. Upon completion of transmission, the DSCIM shall provide a transmission complete\nindication to the transmitting device over a separate\nline. Simultaneously, the DSCIM shall resume scanning other inputs starting at the next sequential\nposition. In all cases, the DSCIM shall insert, in\nthe first seven bit portions of its serial output,\nthe scanning position in straight binary code which\nshall be-correlated, by the DCC computer, with the.\ninput device receiving the DSCHf output.\n\n.J\n\nI\n\nI\n1\n\n\xc2\xb71\n\n1\nj\n\nr-\n\nr\n!\n\nr\n\n,\nT\n\n..\n\n-\'"-\'-\n\nI\nI\n\n- ---<-,.----\n\n,\n\n\'-1\n\nT-\'~~-I\n,\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2 -I\n\nI\ni\n\nl\n\nJSC-IOOI3\n\n4.4.2.9.7 Multifunction Support Requirements. The DSCIM\nshall be capable of supporting a multifunction environment in\nwhich simultaneous active functions, residing in and utilizing up\nto eight DCC computers, will be accepting inputs from the various\ninput devices. In this environment, the DSCIM shall receive a\nfunctior code from the input device with each input, and insert\nthe code in its corresponding output word to the DCC computers.\nEach computer shall receive all DSCIM output words, and extract\nthose words whose function code identify its resident function\n(or functions, if the given computer is configured for multijobbing) .\n4.4.2.10 Command Computer Input Multiplexer (C/CIM) Subsjstem. Two redundant multiplexer channels shall be provided in the C/CIM.\n4.4.2.10.2 Hardware Integrity and Safing. In order to maint~in the integrity of the C/CIM hardware and to ensure the receipt\nof error-free, switch encoded command data by the command proces~or, ~he following C/CIM hardware functions shall exist:\na.\n\nThe true and compliment side of each command module\nswitch shall be sent to its respective encoder.\n\nb.\n\nSwitch closure data shall be routed direct from each\nconsole module on two separate cables. These cables\nshall not go through any console~~iring Distribution\nModule (WDM) or CTC. One cable shall contain the\nPBI "true" data, the other cable shall contain the\nPBI "complement" data.\n\nc.\n\nThe true and complement PBI data shall be compared\nby the C/CIM encoders, and by the command processor.\nThe C/CIM shall not output switch data unless a\ncomparison between the true and complement is detected. Likewise the command processor shall not\noutput commands unless a comparison between the\nC/CIM true and complement is detected.\n\nd.\n\nIn order to prevent address skewing, a minimum of\ntwo bits shall separate each encoder address.\n\ni\n\nI\n\n.j\n\nJ\n\nj\n\n.1\n\ne.\n\nAn even parity bit shall be generated internal to\nthe C/CIM fOT each data word transferred to the\ncommand ~rocessor.\n\n(j)\n\n,."\n\nWbL 7321 \'/76\n\nPAGE\n\n265\n\nr.\n,\ni\n\nf\' -\n\nc_I~"\n\n{\n\nI\n\nI\n\n\\\n\n--.---.".,--\n\n.~\n\n.\n\n"\n\n~\n\n"\n\nI\n\nAeronutronic ~\nAeronutronic Ford Corporancn\nSpace Information Systems Operation\n\nl \'----I\n\n:1\nj\n\n!\n\nI\n\nJSC-l0013\n\n1\ni\n\n!\n\n4.4.2.10.2\nf.\n\nHardware Integrity and Safing.\n\nj\n\n(Continued)\n\nj\n\nA high-speed printer shall be provided for monitoring\nthe CICIM output to DCC.\n\nJ\n\nI\nj\n\n1\n~\n\n4.4.2.10.3 Command Module Types. The COM equipment group\nshall _be capable of transforming digital data from magnetic tape\ninto alphanumeric characters or graphic plots on the face of a\nCRT, an~ shall record this information on microfilm for subsequent\ndisplay on a film reader.\n\na.\n\nMagnetic Tape Unit. The magnetic tape unit shall\naccept 1/2 - inch wide, NRZ 9 -tra\'ck, computer tapes\nrecorded with an 800 BPI density at 37.5 IPS. The\ntape unit shall accept both 8-1/2-inch and 10-1/2inch reels.\n\nb.\n\nComputer Format. The system shall be capable of accepting data assembled in IBM 360 SYS OUT and UNIVAC\n494 computer print formats and DTE output formats\nwithout reformatting by the host computer.\n\nc.\n\nError Detection. The system shall provide the capability of detecting tape read errors and shall mark\nthe frame or page containing erroneous data with a\ndiscrete. symbol(s).\n\n, eOt\n~\n\n~W-O-~-7-32-1-1-/7-6--------------------------------------------------P-A-\'G--E---Z-7-0----------~\n\nr\n\n. . \xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7r-\xc2\xb7\nAeronutronic\n\nr\n\n\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7~r~\n\nI\n\n,\n\n~\n\nd.\n\nCOM\n\nEquipmen~n~.\n\n(Continued)\n\nAlphanumeric Requirements\n(1)\n\nCharacter Set. The system shall provide programmable sets of up to 256 characters consisting of upper case and lower case letters,\nnumerics, and special symbols as required by\nthe various print tape processor programs.\n\n(2)\n\nCharacter Size. Reliability (R) is defined as the probathat a system of equipment can meet an operational objective during a finite interval of time.\n\nbiJ~ty\n\nThe folloiving paragTG\\phs shall be used to specify a numerical reliability requirement for the mandatory equipment strings, to\nenumerate such equipment strings necessary for the successful\nsupport of the Shuttle Orbiter, and to identify fixed redundancies\nthat are independent of mission requirements. The reliability\nestimates obtained from equipment and system evaluations is dependent on groundrules and operational philos ophy deve:~oped on a\nmission-to-mission basis.\n4.6.1 Reliability Requirements. The reliability of each\nstring shall be R = 0.9995 for a time interval equal to the sum\nof the critical m:i.~sion periods occurring at commencement of countdown. for Orbiter launch, continuing th\\ough the orbital test flight,\nand ending at the termination of the flight test. During critical\nphases~ prolonged periods of interrupted control cannot be tolera ted. -While failure criteria vary among various subsystems, it is\ngener<!.lly accepted that failures iVhich can be remedied by immediate\'\nswitchover to standby equipment are not considered system failures.\nConversely, failures which require repair of failed components or\n\xc2\xb7necessitate reinitialization of the system are considered system\nfailures.\n\n,j\n\ni\n\nr\n\ni\nI\nI\n\nI\n4.6.2 Configuration Identification.\nments shall apply to functional stringS-of\nmente The function of the string shall be\nfied. Nonreconfigurable fixed hardware redundancy shall exist for those WBD, lISD, and\nTTY functions that are constant for mission-tomission operation requirements. All equipment\nimplementation, augmentation, or modification should\nbe reviewed from mission-to-mission to ensure that\nthe necessary redundancy is present so the system\nperformance does not degrade below the levels attained\nfor previous missions.\n\nb.\n\nOperational Redundancy. As the HSD is considered\nmandatory only during the launch phase and hardlvare\nredundancy shall exist within the string, no requirement for operational redun.dancy for the HSD elements\nexist. However, critical WBD and TTY data shall be\nrout6~ along independent paths t~ multiple users \xe2\x80\xa2\n.S.ufficien1; operational redundancy, therefore, is\nrequired so that the system performance does not\ndegrade below the levels at taine_d for previous\nmissions.\n\n,\n\n,-,\n\n(.\n\n4.6.2.2\n\nNIP\n\n4-.6.2.2.1 Boundaries. Minimum equipment redundancy shall be provided in the NIP Subsystem elements where sufficient operational functional redundancy exists to assure system\nsuccess. Failover to redundancy channels shall be accomplished\nwithout loss of data.\nI\n\nJ\n\n1\n\n1\n\n1\n1\n:\n\n;I .\n\n(tL\n\n4.6.2.3.1 Boundaries. Analysis of the SDPC shall be limited\nto the requirements specified in the RFP. In response to the RFP,\nthe bidders shall provide a reliability analysis of the system\nconfig-uration that involves creation of graphical reliability\nmodel~, conversion of the graphical models into mathematical mod~\ne\'ls, and the solvin.g of the mathematical model-s to provide the\nreliability prediction.\n\n1\n\n4.6.2.3.2 Criticality. A system string capable of providing\nsupport is composed of a central processor with 3.2 MB of addressable m.emory and direct access storage wi th a minimum storage capacity of 100 MB. A computer operating system is a set\nof programs and routines which guide a computer in the performance\nof its tasks and assist the programs (and programmers) with certain supporting functions. The operating sy.stem for each computer\nin the MCC shall provide the\'environ:ment and the specialized soft~\nware t~ols req~ired by the applications programs.\nThe operating systems used in the MCC shall be standard vendor\nsupplied systems plus augmentations required to satisfy the special MCC demands. All of the large scale operating systems provide the same, or very similar, functional capabilities despite\nthe different hardware architectures and the different design\nphilosophies.\nThe programs and routines of an operating system can be divided\ninto tile fo110\\ving functional groups.\na.\n\nI\n\nJob Management. Responsible for organizing and\nregulating the flow of work in a system by selecting, initiating, and controlling the execution of\ntasks.\n\nb.\n\n1\n\nj\n\nSystem Resource Management. Allocates and maintains\nthe status of resources to tasks and programs selected for execution. Resources typically include\nmemory, CPU time, tapes, disks, printers, timing\nservices, etc.\n\nc.\n\n1\n\nData Management. These functions consist of file\nmanagement facilities, input/output (I/O) support\nfacilities, and data management system facilities.\n\nd.\n\n\'j\n1\n1\ni\ni\n\nj\n\nSystems Management. Concerned with system generation, systems maintenance, program maintenance,\nand compiler interfaces.\n\nI\n\nAlthough all large operating systems are composed of these functional components, this division is probably not suited for the\nd~scription of any specific operating system.\nWOL. 73Z\' \'/76\n\nPAGE\n\n1\n\n309\n!t1\n\n\'\'\';\'\'"-\'1\'"\'\n\nT-,\n\n,\n,\n\nj\n\n_v...._\n\n-<\n\n.\n\n,\n\n-\xc2\xab\n\n:-r\n\nAeronutronic crqJW\n\n<\n\n\\-----\n\n4f\n\n-\n\n\'I\n\nr\n\n}\n\nI\n\nJSC-iD013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Infonnation Systems Operation\n~.2.1\n\nShuttle Data Processing System (SDPS).\n\nTo be provided.\n\nI;\n\nJ\n\n1\n\n1\nI\n\n1\n1\nl\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7..-\'\n\n1\n\n!\n\n1\n\n1\n\n,\n,\n\ni\n\n1\n1\n\n.....\n\ni\n\n- ....\n\nI\n\n1\nWDL 7321 11/73\n\nPAGE\n\n310\n\nr\n\nI\n\nI\n\nr\n\nI\n,\ni\n\n. -1\'-----\n\nI\n\nL\n\n1\n\nAeronutronic ~\n\n.-.~--\'<\'~\n\n...... --\n\n,\n\n1----[--.\n\n-,,-"-\n\n~r\n\nr\n\n(\n\nI\n\nJ5C-10013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpac$ Infonnation Systems Operation\n\n5.-2.2\nprovided.\n\nWDL 7UI 11/73\n\nData Processing Computation Complex (DPCC).\n\nPAGE\n\nTo be\n\n311\n\nT--\'---\'\nI\n\nr\n\nI\n\n,.\n\nJ\n\n!.\n\n--I\n\n\xc2\xb7~~-\xc2\xb7--T~\xc2\xb7-\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\n\n1\n\nt\n\nI\xc2\xb7\n\nl\n\n;\n\n., Aeronutronic\n\nCS1!P\n\nJSC-IOOI3\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Infonnation Systems Operation\n\n......\n\no\n\n5._2.2.1 Enhanced Operating System (EOS). The Enhanced\nOperating System (EOS) is the support system for the System 360\nModel 75\'s in the Real-Time Computer Complex (RTCC).\nThe EOS is based on release 21. 8 of operating system mul tiprogramming with variable number of task (OS MVT) providing multijobbing. The EOS meets the following five goals.\na.\n\nRequires a minimum number of OS MVT captures.\n\nb.\n\nProvides suppo-rt for OS HVT and local services.\n\nc.\n\nProvides an efficient, high performance operating\nsystem for the RTCC.\n\nd.\n\nCompatible with OS HVT support services and program\nproducts.\n\ne.\n\nRequires\'a minimum amount of local maintenance\nsupport.\n\nThe _cont,rol program in the operating system performs supervisory\nand service functions that increase the efficiency of job step\nexecution. These include job initialization, supervision of a\njob throughout its life in the system, and the disposition of the\njob at termination. Hachine malfunctions, including CPU errors, memory errors, and channel errors, are handled by\nthe system recovery facility. The standard recovery procedure is\nto is olate. the cause of the failure, determine if there was a\nhn,rd or\'indeterminant failure, and either abend the task or retry\nthe instruction depending on the type of failure. SRF intervenes and times out all the devices on the failing channel that had active I/O.\nAdditional error recovery procedures are provided to support\nhardHare failures on I/O devices outboard of the 360/75. The\nTPC software shall consist of real-time telemetry preprocessing\nsoftware, systems software, systems test software, and reconfiguration software. The real-time software shall be capable of\naccepting two telemetry downlinks simultaneously. The valid\ncombinations of Orbiter and Payload downlinks are shown in table\n4.\nThe software shall incorporate all the functions necessary to provide a generalized decommutation service for a wide variety of\ntelemetry formats. The Shuttle OD data shall be preprocessed\naccording to various downlink characteristics. The telemetry\npreprocissing software shall be table driven to minimize missionto-mission reconfiguration time.\n5.3.1 Telemetry Preprocessing Software. Telemetry preprocessing shall consist of the total set of program modules (tasks)\nwhich perform all functions related to the input, validation,\nspecial data processing, reformatting, and output of data derived\nfrom the single downlink input to the TPC by the Network Communication_s .Interface (NCI). These tasks shall be totally memory\nresident and shall operate at the highest application task priority level available in the system. Each task shall be assigned a\nunique priority for the purpose o\xc2\xa3 sequencing the order of execution. A functional block diagram of the telemetry preprocessing\ntask is shown in figure 47. If required due to timing considerations, -the telemetry preprocessing tasks or portions thereof shall\noperate in a "privileged" mode of execution to allow direct control of interfaces and/or peripheral devices which might otherwise be controlled by the Real-Time Operating System (RTOS) in a\nless time critical environment.\nThe telemetry preprocessing tasks shall be table driven to the maximum possible extent. There shall be one set of process control\ntables required for each format which can be downlinked during\na specific mission. These table sets shall reside on a mass\nstorage device such as a disk unites) and shall be accessible by\nthe TPC opera.tional program at any time. L~_.\n\nJSC-l0013\n\n(Continued)\n\nbe memory resident. The real\xc2\xb7time reconfiguration task shall be\nrequired to input these tables. If the required tables are not\nmemory resident upon detection of an A/G downlink format change,\na request shall be made to the real-time reconfiguration software\nfor the loading of the required set of tables. In this case the\nprocessing tasks shall be suspended until all tables are loaded\nand the required hardware/software reinitialization has been\ncompleted. The maximum time for reconfiguration due to A/G\nformat change shall be 15 seconds. Processing shall be reinitiated at the beginning of a data cycle. Advisory messages\nshall be generated and queued for output containing relevant\nin~ormation concerning the format change.\n\n"",\n\n)-\n\n,J,\n\nThe real-time interrupt processor gains control and reinitiates\nthe ncr to continue. It also schedules the minor frame processor\nth rou\'gh the RTOS. Minor frames are mul tibuffered. When the NCr\nhas COlllpleted the transfer of an A/G minor frame to the TPC, a\nminor frame input complete interl\'upt is genera ted. The minor\nframe processing task gains control under a high system priority\nand COI1\'lmEmces the minor frame processing. As each minor frame is\nvalidated it is mapped into intermediate data cycle buffers by the\nminor \xc2\xa3rame/data cycle mapping task. The minor frame validation\nand mapping tasks shall be reentrant in order to handle the case\nof near simultaneous minor frame interrupts.\n\n0, .\n\';\n\nI\nI\nI\n\n1\n\nI\n\n.j\n\n1\n\nj\n\n1\n\nThe support tasks such as manual"input, logging, real-time reconfiguration, ,display, advisory processing are scheduled as require\'d\nby the system \'software.\n\n\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\xc2\xb7\n0\n\n>\n\nWOL. 7321 1/76\n\n.- ,\n\nPAGE\n\n336\n\nI\ni\n\nWhen a complete data cycle has been collected, a request shall be\nmade for the data cycle processing task. This section describes the hardware and software tools which shall be provided to test and checkout MCC functions. Included are definitions of terms used as well as how the\nvarious test and checkout requirements shall be met. General test\nand checkout categories include hardwal\'e, software, and validation\ntesting.\n7.2 ~4CC Readiness Testing. MCC mission readiness testing\nis defined as execution of those tests required to verify MCC\nmission \'support capability. Readiness testing is a procedural\nexecution of specific tests such as phase modulation (PH), sub.system, system, and validation tests. These tests are considered\nto be tools that can be selected and executed as appropriate to\ndemonstrate MCC support readiness for a particular type mission.\nA misslon readiness test plan shall be prepared for each mission\ndefining the tests required and test sequence. The following definitions of\nmaintenance testing cover preventive maintenance, unit level testing, sub\'system level testing, and system level testing.\na.\n\nb.\n\nWDL. 7321 1/76\n\n..\n\nPreventive Maintenance Testing. Preventive maintenance testing and checkout is based on the\nrequirement to test hard\\vare for both electronic\nand mechanical performance in order to detect and\nremedy substandard conditions prior to actual equipment failure. Preventive maintenance must be performed continuously on a scheduled basis and, where\napplicable, include periodic replacement of parts\nwhich have a predictable service life. Preventive\nmaintenance testing-may require- special purpose\nsoftware and/or general purpose or unique test\nequipment. A comprehensive preventive maintenance\nprogram for HCC hard\\vare is required in order to\nensure mission support capability and to minimize\neq\\" 1.}j)\'llen t failure during prime support pe riods \xe2\x80\xa2\nHardware Unit Level Testing. Hardware unit level\ntesting is performance testing to a specification\nof a single functional unit such as a magnetic tape\ndrive, line printer, or TV monItor. It may require\na special software program such as original equipment manufacturer (OEM) line printer diagnostic\nsoftware; however, many hardware devices are tested\nat the unit level by standard or special purpose\nhardware test equipment.\n\nPAGE\n\n366\n\nn\n\nr\n\n-r-\'-----\'\n\n\xc2\xab\n\n~\n\nI\n\ni\n\n,-.~\'\n\n,\n\n~r\n\n\'-1\n\n"t\n\n1\n\nI\n,\n1\n\n}\n\n,\n,\n\n!\n\n,Aeronutronic ~\n\nMaintenance Testing.\n\ni\nI\n\nJSC-l0013\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Information Systems Operation\n\n7~4.3\n\n\'\n\n(Continued)\n\nc.\n\nHard\\vare Subsystem Level Testing. Hardware subsystem level testing requires hard\\vare performance\ntesting at the subsystem level. At this level testing does not verify each element of the subsystem\nto specifications. The objective is to me~sure\ncollective performance as a subsystem; i~e., master\ninstrumentation and timing equipment (MITE) subsystem, NOM subsystem, DTE, etc. Hardware testing at\nthis l~vel may require special software programs to\nsupport checkout and testing such as combined opera"- "tional and readiness test (COHART) to checkout DTE\nhardware.\n\nd.\n\nHardware Sys,tem Level Testing. Hardware system\n"level testing requires capability to verify and\nmeasure performance of all hardware \\vi thin a sys tern.\nSystem hard\\vare operation is not normally verified\nby one overall test.\n"\n\nSystem operational integrity is established by execution of all\nhard\\\'lare subsystem tests associated \\vi th the functional sys tern\nand analysis of collective results of these tests. Results of\ntesting must be available in real\xc2\xb7time or nearreal-time, usually\n~ 10 minutes.\nSystem"level testing requires use of special purpose software\nsuch as COHART, CCATS Open Loop String Test (COST), or presimulation program (PRESHO. Example of hardware system level testing\nis CIM/DTE/DTV!DIST system, test. Software to support this level\nof testing must be comprehensive and diagnostic in nature in order\nto facilitate both rapid fault isolation/repair as well as provide rapid verification of satisfactory operation.\nHard\\vare sys tern level tes ts may be used to requalify hardware systerns after equipment modification.\n\n1\n-I\n\nj\n\nWbL 7321 1/76\n\nPAGE\n\n367\n\nn\n\n"\'"\n\nf\n!\n\n,.\n\n!\n\n,\n\n!\n\nAeronutronic E3\xc2\xa7!a\n,l!\n\n\'>.\n\n:~J\n\nJSC-IOOl.3\n\nAeronutronic Ford Corporation\nSpace Infonnation Systems Operation\n\n,\n1.4.4 Maintenance Testing and Checkout Support.
